Gap trading exist for a long time already. For forex, it can only take signal from friday close and sunday open thus very less trade.  
  
I have come up with a EA. A very simple one. I believe improvements can be made for a sharper entry.  
  
Pls improve together.  
  
Test the EA with Daily TF

While out with my horse ( He's great for discussing the Fx market with) we were thinking about my last post here.  
  
In short, after a gap is formed it usually needs to run into S/R for it to turn back and fill. Be it a trendline, "00", pivot, etc. So an EA to catch this would be tough. In less of course your EA was Eye Awareness. Sorry couldn't resist. I love working gaps for their pips. The problem I often run into is not being busy with something else when they form.  
  
Rufus

  * [#20](/thread/post/3327756#post3327756 "Post Permalink")

  * Dec 27, 2009 10:08pm  Dec 27, 2009 10:08pm 

  * [ blott](blott)

  * | Joined Jul 2009  | Status: Trader | [238 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=109256) | Online Now 

Hi All,  
Hope your festivities were stress-free and you're still speaking with your nearest n dearest!  
  
Before anyone jumps into gap trading, I would suggest they research this method thoroughly and obtain data as follows:- draw vertical lines on every Monday bar on a daily GBPUSD chart, for as far back as you care to go and note which way the gap goes from Friday close. If it gaps down 'pretend' to buy, if it gaps up, 'pretend' to sell. Sometimes the gap is only 1 or 2 pips and you may have to expand your view down to a M15 chart.   
  
With the crosshair tool, look to see how many pips you can get as soon as the bar opens, before you get stopped out; allow for spread.  
You could try TP=20-40 & SL either 100 or 60, depending on risk level/choice. Often the gain is in the 100's.  
Write the results down so you get a statistical result. Often the gap is "closed" within one or two H1 bars, but can be longer, depending on what the market is doing. You will get losing trades but I haven't come across two consecutive losing trades yet.  
  
USDCHF is also another good currency, due to its large movements. Other pairs will need to be researched separately as they move differently to GBPUSD/USDCHF.   
  
An EA would need to be back & forward tested, with TP, SL & TS variables. The size of gap is not relevant to the size of profit/loss; I have seen many cases where the gap is only 1 pip or less and the gain has been quite large and other times where the gap has been huge and the trade has lost.  
  
  
Regards,  
  
  
  
Mike

> Hi Mike and AcedUp!  
>    
>  Could you please your information in regards to how your trading the gap (maybe with a screenshot)? TIA!  
>    
>  Are you using pending orders? If so, how are you setting them (# of pips from low/high price)?
> 
> Ignored

  
I dont use pending orders, I will wait about 10mins after market open then place my first set of lots... this gives tolerance for drawdown. I will place my final set of lots as she accelerates to fill. **(SEE THE YELLOW LINES)**  
  
I place a limit order of about 5pips from gapfill. **(SEE THE RED LINE)**  
  
[http://i498.photobucket.com/albums/r...d_up/gap-1.jpg](http://i498.photobucket.com/albums/rr346/Aced_up/gap-1.jpg)  
  
To make a pretty penny you need to use up the risk a bit... I have attached my (massive) account balance with some notes.  
  
[http://i498.photobucket.com/albums/r.../acbalance.jpg](http://i498.photobucket.com/albums/rr346/Aced_up/acbalance.jpg)

> [Quoting bnbb2004](/thread/post/3333384#post3333384 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi Mike and AcedUp!  
>    
>  Could you please your information in regards to how your trading the gap (maybe with a screenshot)? TIA!  
>    
>  Are you using pending orders? If so, how are you setting them (# of pips from low/high price)?
> 
> Ignored

  
Hi,  
If the Monday price gaps down - BUY  
" up - SELL  
  
Execute market order as soon as market opens.  
Gap size not relevant, only direction dictates buy or sell.  
I use GBPUSD & USDCHF. Other pairs will need different settings or may not be suitable.  
  
TP=40  
SL=65 (or depending on your risk appetite)  
  
You may choose to use a TS, if you wish.  
  
Cheers,  
  
Mike  
  
  
PS Check back through old data, manually placing a vertical line on every Monday on Daily chart. With your crosshair tool, see how many pips you can make, in the relevant direction (see above), before you get stopped out. If you write your results down, you will see that it wins more often than loses and hasn't yet (since Jan 2009) had two consecutive losses on those two pairs, but please correct me on that if you find such an instance.

Hi Acedup,  
It is often this very retracement that provides the 40 pips! If I wait too long i miss my 40 pips. Sometimes there is no retracement and it plunges away in the wrong direction, but that's life! ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)  
  
I used to use SL=100 but that was too eye-watering when it went wrong!  
  
Regarding TP, just hang in there. You are nearly always guaranteed 40 pips or so. Just don't look at the screen until the trade closes!  
  
Regards,  
  
  
Mike

> [Quoting Acedup](/thread/post/3336643#post3336643 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi Mike  
>    
>  Thanks for that info

>  The SL, where you have displayed the RED 100s etc... are these stops that were triggered?
> 
> Ignored

Yes, but later I was more accurate and gave the actual SL. It's main use is to show the number of profitable trades compared to losing ones. You will notice that GBPUSD & USDCHF have the highest rate of success.   
  
I'm sure anyone could have made a much better record of trades than I did!   
  
There is a EA strategy builder from [www.forexgenerator.com](http://www.forexgenerator.com)  
which I used to build a gap trading EA. I think it's their Beta version and informs me it will expire within 10 days. Their support is quite helpful and quick to reply.  
  
I told it to trade only Monday and:-  
IF previous bar close > Monday open THEN buy.  
IF previous bar close < Monday open THEN sell.  
  
You can also set TS, if you wish.  
  
  
Cheers,  
  
  
Mike  
  
  
PS Did you check to see how many pips you could get consistently over previous months? Quite often much more than 40 pips available.

The GU gapped about 60 pips this week. I entered at 1.6114, I had my TP set at 1.6177. I had a trade management ea open on a different chart and it closed me at +21 pips, the pair did retrace about twice that but the gap did not close. So with a 15 pip SL this was a successful trade. The EU only Gapped about 20 and it closed to quickly for me.  
  
I should finish with the GU back-testing tomorrow and will post the XLS. Then on to the USDCHF. Its really nice that some people are really making an effort to figure a system out here. Thanks to you all for your time and expertise

  * [#44](/thread/post/3338046#post3338046 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 4, 2010 10:20pm  Jan 4, 2010 10:20pm 

  * [ blott](blott)

  * | Joined Jul 2009  | Status: Trader | [238 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=109256) | Online Now 

Hi All,  
I don't just aim tp close the gap; price often goes much further than the gap. Sometimes small gaps result in huge movements and vice versa.  
Anyone else get 40 pips this morning GBPUSD? Price just scraped my SL of 60 and went up. As I was up and about, I manually moved my SL to break even, then reached profit target of 40 pips. Price went on for another 80 pips, but I had to go out.   
  
It's all about statistics - it wins more often than loses (with GBPUSD/USDCHF at least). The riskier times can be when the gap goes in the same direction as the trend, so you may wish to aim for a smaller profit and use a smaller SL or not trade, or trade with the gap.  
  
Suck it and see!  
  
  
Cheers,  
  
  
Mike

  * [#46](/thread/post/3338440#post3338440 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 5, 2010 1:25am  Jan 5, 2010 1:25am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar119352_4.gif) Acedup](acedup)

  * | Joined Oct 2009  | Status: Trader | [130 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=119352)

Possibly what is at fault is confidence? If I try a new system and strategy where I am not confident I usually freak out and lose... I sugguest you watch the gaps over the coming weeks and watch how they act... then go for a live trade or two.  
  
Ive been developing a strategy and it works because I have the confidence to carry it through... and I am aware of the risks involved.  
  
as Mike says, the gap can go further than fill... but I have been developing my strategy and targets at before gap fill... I wont try to go further until I am 100% confident.   
  
Good luck what ever you decide to do!

Don't worry at failing; simply try again until you get the hang of it.  
Just start with GBPUSD at first.

You may wish to experiment with your own TP/SL levels, but I use TP=40 SL=68.

  * Edited 7:34am  Jan 6, 2010 7:15am | Edited 7:34am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar119352_4.gif) Acedup](acedup)

  * | Joined Oct 2009  | Status: Trader | [130 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=119352)

Hi guys  
  
Ive been working on back dating GBP/USD gaps and looking at their fill ability with drawdown. Now, ive kept the data at **two hours** as I personally will only be able to take two hours and my target pipage is 20pips.  
  
**9 out of 12 of them filled** or reached my target of 20pips without heavy drawdown  
  
**10 out of 12 of them filled** or reached my target 20pips with 1 heavy drawdown.  
  
have a look at the spreadsheet Ive completed with charts.  
  
The data I was using I downloaded from:  
  
<http://ratedata.gaincapital.com/>  
  
The times on the Sun OPEN and Fri CLOSE are as at NY time (GMT -5) incase you find yourself scratching your head. I used the Ask price, did not discriminate against whether it was a buy or sell as far as using the BID or ASK... this is purely for display purposes and may lack a few pips here and there. **The Red on the charts are the GAPs**!  
  
I will go through some more of my fave CCYs this week now that im on a roll ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f44d.png?v=15.1)  
  
All in all.. my sentiment is that with the right risk management and depending if you are in for a gamble... you can make alot of money on these.  
  
Good Luck  
  
  
**muntu ntu** \- I will share my strategy once Im rolling and have worked out my risks properly... Sorting out this data has made me look deeper and more seriously about the risk I am involving with my account.

Yeah gday all ,the best way for me is ,i always open 3 trades to average a good entry point ,i map larger TF for SR lines ,then i have a indi there that performs my trend,i wait for it to turn then place the trade to fill the gap.sometimes i place a stop at the gap coz its the start of a new weekly candle pends on SR and let it ride with a trialing stop...and nother thing with gap on open is the time fACTOR usually takes any longer than 1 hour to fill i close the trade i pay 13 pip [spreads](/brokers/spreads "View Live Spreads on the Broker Guide") of late ,but USD/JPY is only bout 3 but not much of a gap 40 the most by memory ,normaly bout 15-20, dragon is the one that leaps more imo.. i nurse the trade ,i set large stop incase off power failure or computer/internet buggers up, i trade full time and i just discussing that its a efficient trade with very low risk something that FX doesnt have in normal conditions..will post tommorows open i reckon with high liquidity and NFP we in for a ripper least 80 odd bankable pips..but time will tell....

  * [ xorpheus](xorpheus)

Hi everyone  
  
Something I would like to contribute... and I'll start by saying that although there are no actual gaps I agree that there may be something in it simply because lots of people trade it.  
  
If you want to see the price action that occurred during the "gap" get yourself a demo account with [Oanda](/brokers/oanda "View OANDA Broker Profile"), and I think someone else pointed out the web page with live quotes. I have attached a chart (hopefully it works) on which the vertical yellow line represents the start of trading with my USA based MT4 broker. This is actually 12pm on Monday in New Zealand where I am. You can see things actually kicked off at 7am. New Zealand Daylight Time (NZDT) is currently GMT+13 with daylight savings in place at the moment. The only reason it is Sunday in the USA is because the rest of the world is so far ahead of you! *runs for cover* LOL.  
  
I hope some of you find this useful. Thanks for this thread it looks promising. 

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

The gap is created by our broker with the trades from friday close not sure how but they are there ...23 bankable pips today but didnt trade it as icouldnt nurse it today first time ever.........trend has no relevance with a gap trade weekly or monthly support or resistance has no relevance either ,only its the start of a new candle and a ideal entry for the week,sometimes.yes 3 entries u want to trade at $100 a pip i would open the first one $30,$30 then $40.. ... cheers will post my trade when we hav a good 50+ trade..

  * [#100](/thread/post/3416821#post3416821 "Post Permalink")

  * Feb 1, 2010 12:23am  Feb 1, 2010 12:23am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar43541_7.gif) Ronald Raygun](ronald*raygun)

  * Joined Jul 2007 | Status: 33 y/o Investor/Trader/Programmer | [5,016 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=43541)

The thing I've noticed about gaps, especially large 100 pip + gaps, is you can pretty much trade the fibo retracements within the gap. .  
  
I've also noticed, that once the price goes about halfway in a gap, if it doesn't plow through and complete the gap, it will be a very long time until it does.   
  
Overall gap trading I find too unpredictable to generate a system off of, it's similar to using psych points, or candle patterns--It's something to know about, but not something to base your livelihood on. I have yet to see anything on this thread which alters my view. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

getting ready for tomorrow groovers?  
  
i got to thinking about this a wee bit and i could be way out ofline thinking in this direction about this.  
but when people send money internationally, they always get the bid/ask prices at the time of the transaction at the bank.  
(ofcourse its got a wider spread) but seen as friday is still a day the market is open, perhaps most fo the banks international transfers are not yet confirmed, due to arrr the banks not able to profit from the outstanding tranfers, due to actual current price, so i'm thinking that seen as alot of volume is still pending to be finalized, the market reaches the previous close inorder to fill the lots, yeah look i know i'm probly talking about a small amount, but am i? how can we certain of that....  
  
personally when i send money (from bank to bank, NOT a broker) to my home country on a friday i may not get it in my account until tuesday, sometimes on a wednesday  
  
hmmm chocolate pip cookies for breakfast! 

if i used every commercial EA i would be a brazilianare by next week!!!!

  * | Joined May 2008  | Status: do i look confused? | [616 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=70142)

edge1 and others, just for clarification,   
  
i am trading gaps intraday on the 1 min tf.   
  
the minimum gap size i look for is about half a pip.  
  
if the price has moved a certain distance away from the gap i become interested and have bias for the gap being filled. the more gaps there are in that direction, the stronger my bias is. on aud thats about 15-20 pips. on gbp its 30-40 pips.  
  
if the price goes against me i add more positions, and am mostly trading without stops.  
  
the indi drawing the arrows is called gap finder. its a bit messy but we'll have to make do for now.  
  
you'll find it here  
  
[http://www.forexfactory.com/showthre...28#post3446428](http://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?p=3446428#post3446428)

  * [#147](/thread/post/4134136#post4134136 "Post Permalink")

  * Oct 30, 2010 2:42pm  Oct 30, 2010 2:42pm 

  * [ Jack Wasp](jack*wasp)

  * | Joined Oct 2010  | Status: Trader | [22 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=159624)

If anyone's still following this forum here is the strategy I use to trade weekend gaps. It has been very successful to this point.   
  
Strategy:  
-On the Sunday open if a gap of 13 pips or more is present, buy if there is a gap down and sell if there is a gap up. Buy/Sell at market.  
  
-I define a gap as the difference between the Sunday open and the top or bottom of the Friday's candle body depending on the market direction. Example: for a gap down I measure the distance between the Sunday open and the bottom of the Friday candle body.  
  
-Set profit target to 75% of the gap. Set stop-loss to the same. This creates a risk reward ratio of 1:1. Be sure to compensate for your broker's spread.  
  
-I have found these pairs to be the best performers: USD/JPY, GBP/JPY, EUR/JPY, and EUR/USD.  
  
-Take a maximum of three trades. If four setups occur then drop the GBP/JPY. It has the highest spread of the four.  
  
-This strategy can be spread sensitive so look for a broker with low weekend [spreads](/brokers/spreads "View Live Spreads on the Broker Guide") or fixed spreads. I trade this with fixed spreads.  
  
I have attached a spreadsheet which lays out the trades over the last year. Some days there were four setups present but as stated above the GBP/JPY was omitted. I started with a $15,000 balance and set the risk per trade at 5%. That is on the high side of risk but the system has roughly an 80% win ratio. This is a backtest and not the actual trades taken. Hope this helps.  
  

Attached File(s)

![File Type: xls](https://assets.faireconomy.media/images/attach/xls.gif) [GAP BACKTEST.xls](/attachment/file/570648?d=1288417002) 30 KB | 566 downloads

Hi Jack,  
  
I looked into Sunday gap trading (sell on gap up & vice versa) some while back but never did anything about it due to not being able to find a decent EA that would carry out that strategy for me, and would also forget to switch on my computer early enough to catch the first tick!  
  
My back testing shows similar percentage wins to yours, though occasionally three or more pairs would hit SL together to produce an eye watering drawdown. Admitedly, my SL was half yours, so that's where the problem may be. I will attach a simple EA I wrote that trades on Daily bars only; see if it's something you or anyone else could refine.  
  
As prices can sometimes move quickly on Monday opening, I think an EA would be very useful to catch maximum pips, but in your strategy that wouldn't matter.

  * [ Jack Wasp](jack*wasp)

  * | Joined Oct 2010  | Status: Trader | [22 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=159624)

Hi All!   
  
I have spent most of this afternoon going over data from different brokers. I'm far from being done but I have definitely noticed a difference in the results from broker to broker. I ran the backtests on GAIN which performed great. I compared this to my TDFX account and noticed that the results were not quite as good. FXOpen is similar to GAIN on their opening and whatnot from what I can tell. Give me a little time and I'll try to put together some better data for brokers. It seems as if one size doesn't fit all.  
  
fluiDynamic,  
I noticed there was one trade that was open for a couple of days but it did eventually win. Most often though the trades last only a few hours. I have found it best to just let it ride to either a win or loss. Feel free to change TP points to suite your taste. You can't go broke taking profit.   
  
blott (Mike),  
I know how psychologically damaging drawdowns can be. It can create the fear to take even the smallest of trades. The advantages of this system is it has had a fairly high win rate. But, to overcome the mental aspect of three losses on the same day consider reducing your risk percentage per trade. I ran the test with 5% risk per trade. That's high. Find what suits you best. Thanks for the EA. I'll take a look at it.  
  
Looking at my notes there were times that all four pairs triggered but I only took the main three omitting the GBP/JPY due to the spread but had I taken all four I would have fared better. Another possibility would perhaps be to take all four but at say 2% or less per trade. Play with this strategy and take from it what you like best. The only basic rule is that markets tend to fill gaps. By the way as I write this there is a nice gap in the EUR/USD at GAIN.

vukovi,  
The pairs I personally look at and trade for the weekend gap strategy are the EURUSD, USDJPY, GBPJPY, and EURJPY. I have reviewed and studied the performance of the GBPUSD and the EURGBP and found those to not work too well. See post #2645 on Lawgirl's thread for a little more info on that.  
  
[http://www.forexfactory.com/showthre...66#post4135266](http://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?p=4135266#post4135266)  
  
Also keep in mind that there can be periods of several weeks before a trade will setup.   
  
This is only one way of trading weekend gaps. Be creative. For example experiment with going for a larger TP and or SL, find the risk percentage suitable for your personal trading style, etc.   
  
I have discovered that this strategy doesn't perform the same from broker to broker. It depends on what time the broker opens on Sunday's. For example, GAIN opens at 1600 Central time and FXOpen opens an hour later. They both work well for me. TDFX opens at 1800 and doesn't seem to do as well. My advice would be to open demo accounts at various brokers you may be interested in and see if the strategy works by looking back at previous weekends. Also watch the spreads at brokers.   
  
I hope this helps and look forward to seeing you this weekend!

vukovi,

The basic rule of thumb that I use for this is that markets tend to fill gaps. In all my trading in any market, I am always alert when a gap forms. Markets hate gaps.

  * [#160](/thread/post/4149186#post4149186 "Post Permalink")

  * Nov 5, 2010 2:07pm  Nov 5, 2010 2:07pm 

  * [ Jack Wasp](jack*wasp)

  * | Joined Oct 2010  | Status: Trader | [22 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=159624)

Hi vukovi,  
Correct me if I'm wrong but I think you're asking about the risk per trade of 5%. If the gap was a smaller one (10-20 pips) you would increase your lot size but never exceed your total risk per trade. For example:  
  
Gap size=20 pips  
75% target=15 pips  
Risk=15 pips  
Reward=15 pips  
Risk per trade=5% (Use whatever risk is appropriate for you. Use 2% if you feel more comfortable with that.)  
Account size=$1,000  
(I didn't take into account the broker's spread for this example)  
  
Now using the above criteria here is how it breaks down:  
  
Risk=$50 (5% of $1,000)  
Lot size=0.33 or $3.30  
  
Now let's say we had a large gap of say 70 pips. Here is the breakdown:  
  
Risk=$50 (5% of $1,000)  
Lot size=0.07 or $0.7  
  
Either way it will be the same profit or loss. The only difference is the lot size is adjusted accordingly. Hope that helps. Let me know if have any more questions.

Hi vukovi,  
On USD pairs one pip will always equal $10 for a standard lot traded. Other pairs will vary. A mini-lot on a USD pair would be $1. Micro lots would be $0.10. Most brokers have micro accounts available but not all.  
  
Leverage deals with how much margin is required to maintain a position. For example at 100:1 margin on a standard lot on the EURUSD is $1405 whereas 200:1 leverage margin would be $702. Here is a link to a great margin / pip value calculator. It is a free download. You have to submit your email if I remember correctly. It is on the Currensys trading system site. Look towards the bottom.  
  
<http://www.currensys.com/>

Hi vukovi,  
  
First off, you definitely are not boring me to death! I actually enjoy doing this. Now, to answer your question, what broker are you using? Almost every broker I am aware of offers mini and standard lots to be traded in the same account. Some even offer standard, mini, and micro to be traded in the same account. Just be aware that not all brokers work well with the weekend gap strategy. Generally speaking the earlier a broker opens on Sunday's the better.   
  
Now if for whatever reason you are with a broker that only allows you to trade in standard lot sizes, my recommendation would be to always round down on your lot sizes. In your example above of 6.6 lots, I would go with 6. The bottom line is never ever exceed your predetermined risk percentage per trade. And please don't feel you need to risk 5% per trade. It's like I said before, 5% is the high end of risk per trade. If you feel more comfortable go with something smaller like 2%. Most courses on trading recommend no more than 2% risk per trade. There is no holy grail. You will always have loosing trades. It's just the cost of doing business. The idea is to live to trade another day. Let me know if that helps.

> If anyone's still following this forum here is the strategy I use to trade weekend gaps. It has been very successful to this point.   
>    
>  Strategy:  
>  -On the Sunday open if a gap of 13 pips or more is present, buy if there is a gap down and sell if there is a gap up. Buy/Sell at market.  
>    
>  -I define a gap as the difference between the Sunday open and the top or bottom of the Friday's candle body depending on the market direction. Example: for a gap down I measure the distance between the Sunday open and the bottom of the Friday candle body.  
>    
>  -Set...

> Ignored

Hi whatfx,  
  
Yes I have traded this strategy live but just started last Sunday. It did win for me. On one of my accounts a setup triggered in the EURUSD which won.   
  
Over the course of the last year in my other trading styles I kept noticing this Sunday gap happening. In the back of my mind that quite voice kept telling me to take a look into it. Perhaps that was from my days of futures trading. But regardless the voice wouldn't shut up. We had a blizzard up here where I live and I took full advantage of that by locking myself in my office for two days to study. I backtested my theory ran the numbers and was amazed. Does this mean that it will continue performing like this? Absolutely not. This strategy could fall flat on it's face from now on but for that matter any strategy could. All I know is that it has done spectacular over the last year and from my initial analysis it seems 2008 was similar. I will be running the backtests on that soon.  
  
Yes going from demo to live is different. There are two types of differences. The first is obvious; slippage, [spreads](/brokers/spreads "View Live Spreads on the Broker Guide"), etc. The second is not so obvious; emotions. The second is by far the deadliest. The first problem can be dealt with to some degree by finding the appropriate broker for this strategy. The second, well let's just say there are books for this. One thing I have learned is to paper trade until you are tired of being right and not making any money! That will build confidence in your trading plan which will quite your emotions. Emotions and trading don't mix.  
  
I chose a risk to reward ratio of 1:1 because mainly it fits my trading personality. This is partially how I solved the emotions issue. It works for me. I use this ratio in some of my other live trading strategies as well. This risk reward ratio is better suited for something that wins at least 65% of the time. In my opinion, when you go for a risk reward ratio of 2:1 or even higher you can have a series of losses that might not be crippling to your account but they could be crippling to your emotions. Never underestimate your emotions in your trading. I have in the past and it cost me dearly.  
  
As far as the small gap size, my personal strategy for this is I don't like to go after gaps smaller than 13 pips. 13 pips means I would be targeting a 10 pip move. I am testing more of a scalping strategy where one would go after that smaller move. That is still in the works.  
  
GAIN is [Forex.com](/brokers/forexcom "View FOREX.com Broker Profile"). Lucky you being in the UK! You guys don't fall under the ridiculous regulations of the CFTC. A topic for another thread. I was with Forex.com (GAIN) until my account was repatriated to the US. Their Sunday opening is currently 1600 central time which is GMT-5. I am currently using FXOpen for this strategy which opens on Sunday at 1700 central. My best advice would be setup a couple of demo accounts at various brokerages to find which suites you best. This may seem ridiculous but I have at least 10 different demo accounts all from different brokerages. Yes, I have been broker shopping recently.  
  
Sorry about the long post. Hopefully I answered your question. And like I said, stay tuned, I'll be working on more backtests for this strategy. I wanted to have them done for this weekend but I haven't had the time. Take care.

I forgot to answer your question about timeframes. I look at the 30MIN but it doesn't really matter. All you need is the Sunday opening price and the Friday closing or opening price depending upon the direction of the gap. These trades generally seem to last 30 minutes to a couple of hours. There are exceptions. One trade I looked at lasted a day or two if I remember right.

> Hi whatfx,  
>    
>  Yes I have traded this strategy live but just started last Sunday. It did win for me. On one of my accounts a setup triggered in the EURUSD which won.   
>    
>  Over the course of the last year in my other trading styles I kept noticing this Sunday gap happening. In the back of my mind that quite voice kept telling me to take a look into it. Perhaps that was from my days of futures trading. But regardless the voice wouldn't shut up. We had a blizzard up here where I live and I took full advantage of that by locking myself in my office for...
> 
> Ignored

  
thanks for your response.  
  
i did a quick backtest on my broker platform ''ig index''. on the eur / usd pair. thier friday closing time is 9pm GMT, and sunday opening at 9pm GMT also.  
  
ok. what i found is about 60% of the time, the price gaps over 15 pips. these are the only trades that can be taken into account. so taking these trades for 6 trades in the past i got 3 wins and 3 losses.   
  
maybe if i went back a bit more the results could have been different.  
  
also, maybe if i used a different broker the results could have been different also.  
  
but as it stands at present it is break even for the 6 trades. so my thought at the moment is if this gap trading is worthwhile as after about 2-3 months if one hasn't made any pips then its kind of disheartening. after all we are in forex to make pips !  
  
  
anyway keep us posted on your results/findings. and any new ideas about trading the gap or which is the best broker.  
  
also i forgot to mention i had no joy with the other pairs you listed as on ig index those pairs rarely gap for more than 15 pips.  
  
  
regards

> Disliked
> 
> thanks for your response.  
>    
>  i did a quick backtest on my broker platform ''ig index''. on the eur / usd pair. thier friday closing time is 9pm GMT, and sunday opening at 9pm GMT also.  
>    
>  ok. what i found is about 60% of the time, the price gaps over 15 pips. these are the only trades that can be taken into account. so taking these trades for 6 trades in the past i got 3 wins and 3 losses.

> 
> Ignored

I'm glad you looked at your own backtest data. I don't want anyone to just blindly trade this with real money without either demo testing or doing their own backtesting on their broker.   
  
The success of this strategy definitely varies from broker to broker. I ran the backtest on a Forex.com account and actually live trade this on an FXOpen account. So far here is a brief list of brokers that this strategy seems to work on:  
  
Forex.com  
FXOpen  
[FXCM](/brokers/fxcm "View FXCM Broker Profile")  
  
I will update this list as I find more brokers that it fits. I am going to build an ongoing spreedsheet detailing the trades taken that I will post here. The criteria seems to be the following:  
  
-Earlier Sunday open times. Something in the area of 2200 GMT is best.  
-Spreads must be fairly normalized during that time period. For example, this disqualifies [Oanda](/brokers/oanda "View OANDA Broker Profile") because they widen their spreads to 10 over the weekends.  
-The broker must pass at least a brief backtest as compared to the original backtest I ran which I will post again below.  
  
Keep in mind that the period of 9/12/10 thru 10/31/10 the system only took four trades, all winners on a Forex.com account.   
  
Also the way I trade it, my minimum gap size is 13 pips which would then shoot for a TP and SL of 10 pips. Be sure to add your broker's spread.  
  
Compare the data I've compiled in the attached spreesheet with your broker. Demo test this first! Do not risk real money if you are not comfortable with this! Find the risk percentage that is suitable for you. Just because the backtest used 5% does not mean you should. There is absolutely nothing wrong with going with 1-2% risk per trade. Be creative with this. If you find something that works better, by all means let us know. In a market that trades $3.2T plus per day I think there is plenty for all of us to go around.  
  
I will be here this afternoon and post as best I can to keep everyone alerted to what I see. Once again here is the link to prices that should give you an idea of what is happening prior to your broker's open:  
  
<http://www.oanda.com/currency/real-time-rates>  
  
Please review the backtest and strategy in the attached spreedsheet and good luck to everyone this evening (or morning)!

I finally completed the backtests going back to 11/16/2008. I'll be upfront and honest; they are not pretty. While the previous year had a stellar performance the prior 12 months didn't except for one pair, the USDJPY.  
  
I have attached an updated spreadsheet that shows all the data I compiled. Pay special attention to the 3rd tab showing the USDJPY isolated.  
  
Is this still a viable strategy? Yes and no. It depends on what broker you use and the pairs you trade. I will continue to live trade the USDJPY based on what I've backtested. I view this as a strategy to compliment other strategies in your personal arsenal.   
  
If anyone has any ideas on how to improve this, by all means speak up! Afterall we are essentially on the same team with one goal in mind...to make money. Take care.

It could very well be your broker. I ran my two year backtests on Forex.com (GAIN). I actually live trade this with FXOpen. I think [FXCM](/brokers/fxcm "View FXCM Broker Profile") might work but you've got to be careful of the [spreads](/brokers/spreads "View Live Spreads on the Broker Guide").   
  
I agree with you on the GBPUSD. It pretty much fell flat on it's face over the last two years. The EURJPY did great over the last 12 months but wasn't so hot the year before.  
  
For me personally, this strategy is kind of a "beer money" strategy. The trades usually only last on average a few hours if that. Because of the short duration it usually doesn't interfere with my other trading.  
  
I'll keep updating the spreadsheet every week to give everyone an idea of what is happening. It would be helpful if everyone else could post their results with the broker they are using. Good info would include spreads, pairs looked at, and broker's opening time. I can add all that info into the spreadsheet as well.

  * [#211](/thread/post/4287595#post4287595 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 5, 2011 2:51pm  Jan 5, 2011 2:51pm 

  * [ honkin](honkin)

  * | Joined Jan 2011  | Status: Trader | [30 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=165962)

hey guys  
  
It has been an interesting thread to read, as I have been looking for a reliable weekend gap EA for a while now.  
  
There has been some very odd statements made here and there, though. I successfully trade weekend gaps on a regular basis and the only reason I want an EA is I find that at times they can move swiftly and by the time you get it, you can have missed 15 pips or so. I want to be in at market open.  
  
It is also my belief that if you only trade in the direction of the trend, the % increase than when you try to trade countertrend. For me, I look at a 20 day regression channel, but you could use what you wish....long term MA, standard deviation. If the longer term trend is bullish and the candle gaps down on market open, then the long trade is much more likely to be successful. If the long term trend is bullish and the candle gaps up, following the trend, then the countertrend gap trade is much more risky and prone to failure.  
  
If someone had an EA that would allow for a minimum gap size (for me 20, no value if smaller), accurate entry conditions ie if candle open > candle close of last period, enter short at market. The reverse for <  
  
Can set stops and targets if desired and lot size or %. I did like the idea of stop and target being either in pips or % of gap. Ability to handle 5 digit broker.  
  
I am a bit luckier in that market open here is 9am my time, as I am in Australia, so the management of the trade is not so relevant........just the entry. Too hard to monitor a dozen pairs all at entry. For me, that's the part that needs automating. Once in the trade, MyFX Console handles the trade anyway.  
  
I want to be in at market open with a market buy/sell order and I'd like to be able to run it on multiple pairs. I have found no pair any better than another. USD/CAD is as good as EUR/USD, NZD/USD or EUR/GBP. Just watch your [spreads](/brokers/spreads "View Live Spreads on the Broker Guide"). Thankfully, my spreads are never above 3 or 4 at Monday open, though in normal times, between 0 and 2.  
  
I'm sure most of us want a similar end, people. For me, it is just about the speedy entry at open. For others, it may be trade manegement. In the end, we all want to consistently make profits from gap trading. Surely we can pool our collective idea and come up with a reliable EA.  
  
I really do hope we find a decent EA for this. If not, I might have to pay the guys at MQL5 to write me one, as they are great.  
  
All the best in your trading  
  
honkin

  * [#218](/thread/post/4291570#post4291570 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 8:50pm  Jan 6, 2011 6:51pm | Edited 8:50pm 

  * [ roundrock](roundrock)

  * | Joined Feb 2010  | Status: J16 Student | [902 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=132206)

it uses SMA for determining the trend. you dont want any trend indicator set it to false. If userTradingAllowed is false, it doesnt send orders, it just acts like indi  
  
place this EA on any symbol DAILY chart and let it run. it scans all symbols and lists the gaps above min required in the Comment section and places ordrers. it doesnt do exits right now. unless i know exit strategy i cant code.  
  
if you try to backtest, it works for that symbol ONLY. thats a limitation on MT4. You cant backtest multipair strategies...  
  
pl use and let me know any issues.

  * [#220](/thread/post/4291888#post4291888 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 6, 2011 8:25pm  Jan 6, 2011 8:25pm 

  * [ roundrock](roundrock)

  * | Joined Feb 2010  | Status: J16 Student | [902 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=132206)

> [Quoting dr_who](/thread/post/4291619#post4291619 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> D'you think a reasonable exit strategy would be a user-defined X% of the gap and a Ypips SL ? Although this would be simple to include in MPTM which could be used to close the trades.
> 
> Ignored

it could be like that. earlier i tried 75% of gap as TP and 1:1 for SL, it hit SL most of the times before hitting the TP  
  
problem with gap theory is it says gaps do get filled but it doesnt say when. it could take few weeks in some cases. leaving it withput SL is certainly dangerous.  
  
like most of the strategies that 'look' good on paper but get lost due to improper exits, this is also in same category. without a proper exit strategy idea will remain as idea but not as a tradable system

  * [ Kowalczyk](kowalczyk)

I do sometimes trade Gold on Sundays. Every time their is a large move right on the open of the futures session (6 PM EST), gold always retraces back to the last close price. I know with [Oanda](/brokers/oanda "View OANDA Broker Profile"), if EURUSD is down or up alot, you can buy or sell gold right before 6 PM EST at the same weekend prices and make a huge profit on the highly probable move. Then I reverse the position and gold usually goes back to the opening price.   
  
In the following picture. EURUSD was down (Open of 12.26.2010). You would sell gold right before it open at 6 PM EST (you can with oanda). Then after you notice signs of a reversal, you would reverse your position and take profit at last Fridays close. This could lead to some huge profits but make sure to manage your risk.

  * [#231](/thread/post/4297431#post4297431 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 8, 2011 11:14am  Jan 8, 2011 11:14am 

  * [ Kowalczyk](kowalczyk)

  * | Joined Jan 2011  | Status: Trader | [851 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=166317)

> [Quoting whatfx](/thread/post/4297370#post4297370 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> dont understand this ?   
>    
>  also, each broker has different opening time for gold. so the gap times will vary.
> 
> Ignored

Oanda lets you trade virtually 24/7 (yes, you can place trades over the weekend but the [spreads](/brokers/spreads "View Live Spreads on the Broker Guide") are higher and their is no movement).  
  
With that said, EURUSD usually start moving around 2:00 PM on sunday with oanda. So at 5 PM, while most other brokers start trading, you could have been trading with oanda for 3 hours already. But that is besides the point, all you need to know is you can trade 24/7 with oanda.  
  
Now with gold, the official gold market doesn't open until 6 PM on sunday. That means that their is no price movement and with most brokers, you can not trade until 6 PM when the gold market officially opens. However with oanda you can trade before 6 PM. Their are 2 ways you can trade gold.  
  
The first way is more risky. If at 5:45 PM Sunday you see that EURUSD is down more than ~40 pips from fridays close, then you would sell gold right before the Gold market opens (because if EURUSD is down a lot, their is a high probability gold will shoot down.) And you would buy gold if EURUSD is up more than ~40 pips. The reason is that EURUSD show the current value, but since the gold market did not open yet, you would be trading last fridays gold prices. This is the first way, it is a lot more risky but the rewards generally outweight the risk. Make sure to test first.  
  
The second trade you can make is wait for gold to spike up or down. For example in the picture I provided, gold spiked down. Once I saw that it started reversing, I would buy and have my take profit at the original opening price. The reason for this is that whenever gold has a large movement upon open, it always tends to go back to the original opening price.   
  
In short, with the first trade, you are trying to catch the gap using the EURUSD to know if it will go up or down. The second trade is trying to catch the retrace back to the opening price.   
  
A couple of rules. Start trading on sundays. If you are good, you could move on to regular days as well. For the first trade, if their is no major move in EURUSD by the time gold opens, do not trade. And for the second trade, if gold does not spike up or down, do not trade. Their will always be tomorrow.  
  
And you will need to trade on oanda (or any broker that lets you trade 24/7 including the weekends)

When we talk about gold and the gold market, most people refer to futures because they dominate the market. Gold futures are open Sun 6 PM --> Friday 5:15 PM and are closed everyday from 5:15 PM --> 6:00 PM. That is why their is virtually no movement during the weekends and everyday from 5:15 to 6:00 PM and most brokers suspend gold trading overall. That is also why most brokers don't allow gold trading till 6 PM on sunday and why their is a very large movement on sunday at 6 PM.  
  
As for spreads, with oanda, I have never seen the spread more than $5 (even for temporary spikes). On the weekend up to the open, you could expect a $2.5 spread which, generally speaking, is huge but remember that their is usually a very large movement right after the open (up to $20 one way).   
  
I always use limit order just in case. Spikes shouldn't be a problem with but it is better to be safe then sorry.  
  
The importaint thing is patience. Their are weeks where their is little volitility and no spike at all. It is better to wait and fight another day. And make sure to watch / demo with oanda for atleast 3 months before trying it out. I suggest only trading on sunday but it also works on weekdays sometimes.

hi  
  
the chart you posted above is that of eu and not gold.  
  
the problem i see with gap trading on gold is this:  
  
during weekdays there are hardly any significant gaps between day close and open. in fact i could not see any weekdays gaps in the last 2 months on gold.  
  
similarly weekend gaps rarely occur. i only came across one gap of 6 pips in december and one gap in january 2011.   
  
problem is, the gap is so small it is hardly worth trading. it can also be the case that the price may not retrace back to cover the gap. although the majority of the times it does , sometimes it doesn't and just keeps on going one way.....which leaves the question of where to put the stop, and concerns on large drawdowns. just for the sake of a few pips.  
  
so iam curious to know how you exactly trade these gaps and some chart examples would help. how many gaps on average do you trade per month on gold ?  
  
today, there was no weekend gap on gold.

> Ignored

A couple of thing I think that you misunderstand and I will try to explain myself better.  
  
First of all, XAU/USD is the symbol for spot gold in USD. So the chart I provided is the price of gold when it opened on Dec. 26th.  
  
Second of all, I meant this strategy should primerily be traded at the start of the week (on Sunday). I have trade this strategy over the last year and a half and I rarely trade on the weekdays, only when EURUSD make a huge move (you can use other USD pairs to confirm that the value of the USD is changing not the EUR, but this is really unnecesary)  
  
Now let me talk about the opening price of gold. In the chart I provided, Gold initially opened about $6 lower but soon traded as much as $12-$13 lower before it showed a sign of a reversal. Now I am not sure if you traded gold before but $13 on gold is a lot, especially within an hour.   
And that is only one way. Remember, you are trading on the original movement and also the retracement. So realistically, you would have made $20 of gold on that day.  
  
As for number of trades a month, it really does depend. Sometimes it is 2 or 3 times and some months I don't trade at all. But when I do, I know that their is a very very high probability that my trade will be favorable and profitable. The thing is, you really only need to be in front of the computer for 2 hours a week (if you only plan on trading sundays, recommended for starters).  
  
Today, I did not trade. EURUSD had made a move but when Gold opened, it was nearly unchanged. And Gold did not make a large move when it opened so their was no retracement trade today either.  
  
You also said that the price sometimes doesn't retraces back to the open, personally I have never seen this on a sunday (I have misses a couple of weeks). I have although seen this on weekdays. I forgot to mention this but you NEVER EVER EVER trade the retracement on weekdays, only on weekends (Sorry, I know this was importaint). For weekdays, you would only trade if their is a HUGE move in EURUSD. But you never trade the retracement on the weekdays, only the original move.  
  
And this leaves us just one question left unanswered. Once you see the signs of a reversal, you place a trade with you take profit just below last fridays close price (a bit below because of the spread) You should place your stop just below the low or above the high gold made. If your stop get hit, that means you will make even more on the retracement so don't be too pissed about it (rarely gets hit). And if your stop is hit 3 times, I would recommend cutting your losses (this never happened and doubt it ever will. Gold would need to drop $50 for this too happen and the chances of that are nearly impossible).  
  
Make sure to use a 15 minute chart to look for reversals. I will post charts later when I find more time. For now, good luck with all you trades.  
  
And I believe 6 PM EST is 11 PM london time. So you would start at 10:45 PM (22:45) london time.

cheers roundrock. A shame. I often find no gaps in my daily charts, but they are certainly there in 1 minute or 5 minute charts.  
  
9am Australian time today as follows:  
  
GBP/AUD Close 1.5614 Open 1.5637 Gap not quite closed yet, currently 1.5631  
EUR/USD Close 1.2907 Open 1.2878 My Trade Result +24  
USD/JPY Close 83.15 Open 83.24 Didn't take it as under 20 pip gap. Trade went on to fill the gap and continue to 83.06 in 42 minutes.  
AUD/USD Close 0.9958 Open 0.9928 Trade Result +26  
AUD/CAD Close 0.9919 Open 0.9861 Gap not filled, but I exited at .9896 for a Trade Result +30  
EUR/CAD Close 1.2824 Open 1.2790 Trade Result +26  
  
Some spreads kill you a bit with these trades so early, but mine don't hit past 4 or 5. Most are around 2 until trade really gets going and then between 0 - 2  
  
There were more under 20 pips, so left them alone.  
  
Such a shame your EA is for daily charts only. Might have to test it anyway and get inside and tweak it for 5 minute charts  
  
Why wouldn't you want to automate trading these little money spinners? As a supplement to your trading, they are great. It's just a pain to monitor so many and enter at market  
  
cheers

> The first way is more risky. If at 5:45 PM Sunday you see that EURUSD is down more than ~40 pips from fridays close, then you would sell gold right before the Gold market opens (because if EURUSD is down a lot, their is a high probability gold will shoot down.) And you would buy gold if EURUSD is up more than ~40 pips. The reason is that EURUSD show the current value, but since the gold market did not open yet, you would be trading last fridays gold prices....

  * [#245](/thread/post/4308116#post4308116 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 13, 2011 1:50am  Jan 13, 2011 1:50am 

  * [ JFogel](jfogel)

  * | Joined Dec 2010  | Status: Trader | [39 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=164716)

The best "Gap" strategies are really just natural tendencies. For example, the EURUSD opens lower at the Sydney Open than it did on Friday's close roughly 65% of the time. However, when the market does open lower during the Sydney Open, it continues to drop for about 4 hours 70+% of the time. However, the Sydney open has little effect on most other currencies. One strategy usually only works with one currency, not every market and every interval. Be sure to backtest these theories so you can have a better view of the market as a whole rather than being led blindly.  
  
Happy Trading :-) 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [ Kowalczyk](kowalczyk)

  * | Joined Jan 2011  | Status: Trader | [851 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=166317)

> [Quoting shandy](/thread/post/4304232#post4304232 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi Kowalczky,  
>    
>  Interesting strategy. So is 40 pips the "magic number"? I notice on Sunday EURUSD had gapped down ~33 pips, but XAUUSD moved up on open according to my MT4 broker chart. Did you trade this?
> 
> Ignored

Although EURUSD did go down as much as ~33 pips, at 5:45, it was only down about 10 pips, so I would not have traded. Also, their was no spike when it opened so I wouldn't trade the retracement either. It has to be down or up atleast 40-50 pips at 5:45 (the more the better). The basic principle behind this strategy is that is EURUSD is down more than 40 pips, the USD got stronger, therefore gold (vs. the dollar, XAU**USD**) should make a large move down also.

  * [#247](/thread/post/4309088#post4309088 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 11:00am  Jan 13, 2011 8:00am | Edited 11:00am 

  * [ Kowalczyk](kowalczyk)

  * | Joined Jan 2011  | Status: Trader | [851 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=166317)

> [Quoting whatfx](/thread/post/4300422#post4300422 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> i see. the question of stop is extremely important. you say if you are trading the retracement up, then the stop should be just below the low. but the low will be about the same point you entered trade ! also not sure what you mean by 3 stops being hit ? that would be a disaster and will take months of weekend gap trading to recover.  
>    
>  i have seen one weekend where the price never retraced but kept on going one way, that one trade itself would have thrown you back a few months. so i think this needs to be given a thought.
> 
> Ignored

I will try to reexplain myself using the chart I posted. The 4th candlestick was a doji followed by a large bullish candlestick. That is a reversal signal. You would close your short position and enter long. Your stop for the long position would below the 5th candlestick (because it reached the lowest point before the reversal).  
  
Now lets say gold went even lower, your stop would be hit. Then you would wait for another reversal signal (do not enter a short position). Once you see a reversal signal, you would enter long with your stop below the new low.   
  
If your stop got hit again you would repeat.  
  
If your stop gets hit 3 times (I have never seen this happen), you would just stop trading and cut your losses. The thing is, if your stop got hit 3 times, you would lose $10-$15 dollars on gold, but if your trade is sucessful, you would make atleast $20+ on gold so even if your stops get hit 3 times, your not really in trouble.  
  
The great thing about this strategy is that if you stop gets hit once or even twice, you would make even more money because the retracement would be a lot larger, so don't get mad.  
  
Also, could you please provide a date or chart of a time when gold never retraced.

sure. gold never retraced on the weekend of 20/12/2010. opened up with a gap. never retraced back down to fill the gap. so you would have been stopped out here on whatever stop level you entered.  
  
also, i did a quick backtest on alpari. hardly any gaps come about and those that do are not worth trading:  
  
  
  
27/9 - no gap - no trade  
  
4/10 - only 1 pip gap - no trade  
  
11/10 - 4 pip gap. not worth trading - after spread - no trade  
  
18/10 - 2 pips gap - no trade  
  
27/10 - no gap - no trade  
  
1/11 - 5 pips gap. possible trade but just 1/2 pips to be made !  
  
8/11 - 2 pip gap - no trade  
  
15/11 - 1 pip gap - no trade  
  
22/11 - 3 pip gap - no trade

27/12 - 4 pip gap - no trade  
  
31/12 - no gap - no trade  
  
10/1 - no gap  
  
  
  
so my friend, i cant see any single gap trading oppurtunity in the last 2.5 months . i would like to see where you get your figures from, and what results you have had.  
  
  
  
also, you say on the opening of the gap, you wait for the market to move in the same direction, then after a reversal occurs then enter trade. but what if reversal occurs on the opening of the gap itself ?  
  
  
  
for example, say gold opened with a gap 'UP' by 8 pips. so we would need to enter short so that when gold retraces back down our gap would be filled and we would win the trade. but you say to wait for gold to go up more before entering a short. and once its gone up and then reverses back down, then to enter short.  
my question to you is, when gold opens on the gap, what if it immediately goes back down ? does not go up. when would we enter short ? we wont have a chance to because we will be waiting for the market to go up before entering short, which it never did. and we would have missed our short. what do you do then ? this occurs a lot. prime example on the 1/11/2010.  
  
  
also, what about stops ?? sometimes market goes up/down by even 15 or more pips before filling the gap !  
a huge amount of pips to lose just to make 6-7 pips when the gap fills, and there is no guarantee the gap will fill.   
  
  
so, i would like to see your results and what you do. because i cant see how this would work...  
  
  
regards

hi... weekend gap does not show and backtest results. of i'm doing plotting it wrongly....  
  
my strategy very simple... i wake up at the start of the day on sunday night or monday morning at my timezone and will monitor those mt4 screens with high gaps using TF Daily . if yes i open trade... normally i would max out with the TP right up to the close of last week candle...as history tells that gap always closes the windows exactly for major pairs and crosses. As for the exotic pairs... i have no idea to trade gap or even brave enough to trade them as it looks a bit scary due to their spreads and not having a good history for closing gaps.  
  
cheers!!!!....

gaps on ibfx are quite different than say gaps on gomarket or [fxpro](/brokers/fxpro "View FxPro Broker Profile").

> I will try to reexplain myself using the chart I posted. The 4th candlestick was a doji followed by a large bullish candlestick. That is a reversal signal. You would close your short position and enter long. Your stop for the long position would below the 5th candlestick (because it reached the lowest point before the reversal).  
>    
>  Now lets say gold went even lower, your stop would be hit. Then you would wait for another reversal signal (do not enter a short position). Once you see a reversal signal, you would enter long with your stop below the...

Sorry, I was busy this week. I would not have, and will not traded this week. Their was no major movement in the USD before gold opened and their was no strong movement. If you look at the 15 min. chart, gold did make a ~$5 movement but the candle closed more than halfway down. The next candle was bullish but failed to make new highs. And the third candlestick was bearish and went lower than the previous candlestick. This shows that there is / was no strong movement. And even though gold is making new highs as I type this, its better to play it safe than sorry, so I will not be trading today. As we clarified before, these opportunities are few and far between, but when they do occur, they are almost a guaranteed profit.  
  
As for the dates you provided earlies, I will try to look over them later this week.

  * [#263](/thread/post/4356923#post4356923 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 31, 2011 10:41am  Jan 31, 2011 10:41am 

  * [ Kowalczyk](kowalczyk)

  * | Joined Jan 2011  | Status: Trader | [851 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=166317)

Today was a good day for trading gold. Gold opened trading up. Saw a dojo at 19:00 (on the 15-min chart) and gold went downhill from there.   
I was short at 1344.30 and took profit at 1339.25 for a profit of $5.05. Odds are it will go lower to ~1337 (bid+ask/2) but I decided to secure my profit.  
  
Also, you could have traded the initial move. In this instance it would be different. Obviously, because of the Egypt debacle, gold and the USD are becoming stronger. So since people were putting money into th USD, it only made sense they put money into gold too. I know this goes against the rules but given the riots in Egypt, you should not have shorted gold on the open. The safest play is to just stay out (which is what I did).

Then I started trading the initial move too. However times have apparently changed. Currently, Gold goes the direction of the EURUSD about 65% of the time. So for now, you might only want to play the retracement, not the initial move.

  * [#297](/thread/post/4550554#post4550554 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 18, 2011 5:52am  Apr 18, 2011 5:52am 

  * [ Mementocom](mementocom)

  * | Joined Dec 2008  | Status: Trader | [5 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=89318)

My broker allows trading from 20:00 GMT on Sunday until 22:00 GMT Friday  
In most Mt4 platforms market opens at 23:00 GMT (my time)  
  
Extra 3 hours...  
  
So I'm looking at 2 gaps, from 2 different brokers, one at 20:00 another at 23:00  
Gaps are great for using  
1) Filling gaps, my statistics show that the most probable outcome is 78,8% of gap range.  
2) Also I am using it to reverse a position a the top/ bottom of a gap.  
3) Or if there is a nice big bullish/bearish candle I will keep a position for larger move..statistics show that it have an importance on the future price action (use it not only to fill a gap)

  * [#299](/thread/post/4550565#post4550565 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 18, 2011 6:05am  Apr 18, 2011 6:05am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar153883_26.gif) PoundTrader](poundtrader)

  * Joined Sep 2010 | Status: Life Time Member | [6,685 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=153883)

there is no such thing as gap, the market keep moving during the weekend, the gag comes from where your broker close on friday and where it open on sunday, so if your broker close on friday at 1.5505 and the market is moving during the weekend and price is at 1.6505 and your broker opens at that price you think it's a gap but it's not

There are many ways of investing money...this one is pretty simple  
This "Weekend Gap" is just an empty space on a chart...the most important thing is this: It really works!  
  
The best way to learn any method is to analysis it..a lot!  
  
You may not like it, but many trade it with great success.

<http://i54.tinypic.com/286xuso.jpg>  
  
This for instance is not a gap for me... yesterday gap on eurusd had only 2 points...I search for gaps a least 5 point  
Enter them as soon as spread is normal  
on EurUsd I have 10p. spread at open  
after 20-minutes it gets normal to 2p.  
the same with other pairs  
  
Remember look at 3-4 brokers to compare gaps  
Remember the bigger the gap the better (look for 10pips or more)

  * [#305](/thread/post/4554141#post4554141 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 19, 2011 12:50pm  Apr 19, 2011 12:50pm 

  * [ optojay](optojay)

  * | Joined Apr 2009  | Status: Trader | [94 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=101371)

Memento - what kind of stop loss do you use when trading the gap(say you target 75% of the gap as your TP)?  
or do you close on time expiry?  
  
I used Pircj EA (Sunday Gap Trader v1) to backtest - you can specify TP and SL based on a percentage of the gap. (I optimized backtests of TP = 25% to 200% and SL = 1 to 4 times the TP)  
  
Some results were amazing and others were horrible. Furthermore, they were not consistent across pairs. I lose confidence in the trading strategy when such strong optimization is needed to get good results - essentially curve fitting to each pair.  
  
Thus my question regarding your SL if you find much success trading gaps. Thanks for the comment re:waiting 20 minutes for spreads to come down before entering.  
  
Thanks!  
  
If anyone is interested, Pircj included code(but had it deactivated) for trading his EA by AccountBalance instead of FreeMargin. Here is the EA where risk is based on AccountBalance instead of FreeMargin. 

Attached File(s)

![File Type: mq4](https://assets.faireconomy.media/images/attach/mq4.gif) [Sunday Gap trader V1 AB.mq4](/attachment/file/682556?d=1303184747) 8 KB | 837 downloads

C'mon, gap traders! is gap trading dead? nobody gap traded since april, even those huge gaps this week end? I took the one on nzd/yen, for a mere 20 pips Could have got the double, but my hands shooke .  
One question now: why do some gaps close and others not? how do you tell which will do what beforehand? I am sure there is a way. But for now I just play gaps to close, but noticed that when they don't, they explode to the opposite direction.  
  
best,  
Muntu

  * [#307](/thread/post/4814200#post4814200 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited Jul 28, 2011 12:30am  Jul 27, 2011 9:55pm | Edited Jul 28, 2011 12:30am 

  * [ Krumpip](krumpip)

  * | Joined Jul 2011  | Status: Trader | [18 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=187742)

Ive been trading the sunday gap for over a year now and i ask myself the same question. Some brokers closing time on Friday differ by an hour and often there is quite alot of movement in the last hour so this affects the gap. Daylight saving and public holidays also affect gap performance. I dont trade gaps the week London or New York wind their clocks forward or back for Daylight saving. Any other ideas?

My beginner's question to gap-traders. Would the following strategy work? :  
  
Pending buy/sell-stop orders are placed during last minute(s) of broker's Friday night, just before weekend closure. Distance between orders would be around 10-15pips and there would be proper SL/TP targets. Pairs of choice would only be eurusd, gpbusd, audusd and usdchf.  
  
Then during the first opening minute of monday sufficient move would spike through and activate one of pending orders, off cource providing that there is no slippage with pending order execution. If there is no sufficient gap during first seconds, orders would be manually closed.  
  
Am I missing something here? 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#313](/thread/post/4947394#post4947394 "Post Permalink")

  * Sep 12, 2011 9:40pm  Sep 12, 2011 9:40pm 

  * [ LucianoDolce](lucianodolce)

  * | Joined Sep 2011  | Status: Trader | [33 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=194459)

Especially since you are relying on zero spreads when the market opens on Monday, which is almost impossible.   
  
What I think is missing in you plan is getting prepared to the case in which the gaps is opened against you-that is very dangerous.   
  
If you want to trade gaps, dont try to predict whether a gap will be opened or not. Wait till it is opened and then try to take the currency to the gaps closing levels (gaps tend to be closed eventually) .  
  
Good Luck ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

  * [#335](/thread/post/6064224#post6064224 "Post Permalink")

  * Oct 3, 2012 3:40pm  Oct 3, 2012 3:40pm 

  * [ blott](blott)

  * | Joined Jul 2009  | Status: Trader | [238 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=109256) | Online Now 

Hi Everyone,  
  
Be careful when you trade gaps. Sometimes price just keeps on going. Then, where do you put your SL i.e. how deep are your pockets? One hit SL could wipe out all your gains, then you have to wait another whole week to claw a bit back.  
  
It's better if it gaps during your daytime hours, then you can maybe watch it and catch more pips when price has exhausted itself and starts to head back towards the gap.  
  
If price gaps completely outside the Friday range, then it usually keep s on going, so just trade WITH the gap.  
  
Cheers,  
  
  
Mike 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#336](/thread/post/6065040#post6065040 "Post Permalink")

  * Oct 3, 2012 7:41pm  Oct 3, 2012 7:41pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar98258_3.gif) Muntu](muntu)

  * | Joined Mar 2009  | Status: Trader | [448 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=98258)

Frani's chart illustrates one problem with gap trading that in my view relates to SL question put by Blott: as with any other method, gap trading is better done in a trending market. If the trend is there, I prefer the gap to go against it. I then enter when the trend resumes and put my sl below the lowest point reached by the gap, if long. This way you can remain in the trade for a couple of days at times. At least this is the way I play it: the must close then continue some.  
  
The market opening gap can offer one of the best times for a very tight SL, IMHO, but risk is always there, so always take it easy.  
  
BTW I am still in my E/U trade, though not very far. My SL is at BE and ... we'll see 

Patience is magic

  * Oct 10, 2012 4:12am  Oct 10, 2012 4:12am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar105477_2.gif) newschool](newschool)

  * | Joined Jun 2009  | Status: Trader | [29 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=105477)

Do you make the difference between novice gaps VS pro gaps?  
Not all gaps are good to trade, especially when you take into account the supply/demand levels.  
Here is a video from Sam Seiden (perhaps somebody knows him?) that explains the difference between those 2 types of gaps.   
It really helped me when I was starting.  
  
I posted it here [http://www.forextradingnomad.com/how...ices-and-pros/](http://www.forextradingnomad.com/how-to-trade-forex-gaps-difference-between-novices-and-pros/)

Thanks for sharing, but I find that all those categories are only seen in hindsight , same as continuation or exhausting gaps. You can't tell at the opening which gap will turn what, imho.

  * [#354](/thread/post/6088207#post6088207 "Post Permalink")

  * Oct 11, 2012 4:41pm  Oct 11, 2012 4:41pm 

  * [ angelnish](angelnish)

  * | Joined Jul 2012  | Status: Trader | [29 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=273326)

As you know, I make it a point to trade "The Gap" every Friday. While I missed my specific trade last weekend, I got caught with two open orders. The both gaped in the correct directions giving me $400+ profit.  
  
I liken the Forex to a river. It's level is constantly changing throughout the week from people getting in and out. Over the 48 hour weekend, it settles or moves into equilibrium. Thus, a gap is formed.  
  
It's just an easy way to look at it. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#355](/thread/post/6119363#post6119363 "Post Permalink")

  * Oct 22, 2012 4:41am  Oct 22, 2012 4:41am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar105477_2.gif) newschool](newschool)

  * | Joined Jun 2009  | Status: Trader | [29 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=105477)

> [Quoting Muntu](/thread/post/6084926#post6084926 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Thanks for sharing, but I find that all those categories are only seen in hindsight , same as continuation or exhausting gaps. You can't tell at the opening which gap will turn what, imho.
> 
> Ignored

Can you explain your point more?  
The goal in forex trading, or basically all type of trading is to have a definitive % chance of being in profit. You just need to win 51% of the time to be profitable... (compare this to 49% at best if you go to the casino, with something like Roulette)  
  
So by making the difference between pro and novices gaps, and choosing which one to trade by looking at simple things like support/resistance and trend, its possible to increase the overall % chance of being right. Of course we are not aiming at 100% success, but if you can go to 75% that is already very nice.  
  
Anyways market will open in approx 1 hour for me, and I just wanna share a way to have access to pre-market quotes for free with a demo account from [Oanda](/brokers/oanda "View OANDA Broker Profile"). I just made a quick explanation video about it = [http://www.forextradingnomad.com/for...otes-for-free/](http://www.forextradingnomad.com/forex-live-pre-market-quotes-for-free/)

  * Oct 22, 2012 9:18pm  Oct 22, 2012 9:18pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar98258_3.gif) Muntu](muntu)

  * | Joined Mar 2009  | Status: Trader | [448 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=98258)

In my opinion there is no guaranteed way of saying that a gap, especially an exhausting gap is of such category until the trend reverses and goes against the gap. But maybe I still have some practice ahead.  
You don't need to be right 51% of the time, although preferable, you only need your profits when you win to outweigh your losses.

  * [#357](/thread/post/6134011#post6134011 "Post Permalink")

  * Oct 26, 2012 8:50am  Oct 26, 2012 8:50am 

  * [ kmfx](kmfx)

  * | Joined Oct 2012  | Status: Trader | [5 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=306174)

It's an interval which represent on areas where no trading takes place. It has two trends upward and Downward trend.  
  
Upwards, it is shaped while the highest price of one day is less than the lowest price of the following other days.   
  
Downwards, it produced a gap while the lowest price of one day is higher than the highest price of the following days.

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar105477_2.gif) newschool](newschool)

  * | Joined Jun 2009  | Status: Trader | [29 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=105477)

Hey, market will open in 30mins for me (my broker opens 1h early), so I already checked some pre-market quotes ([I explained here how to get them for free ](http://www.forextradingnomad.com/forex-live-pre-market-quotes-for-free/)).  
  
Looks we won't have any major gaps, most volatility I see is on the Pound, GU and GJ are almost breaking out Friday's closing price. Might be a good time to short.  
Notice that shorting is much better than buying during high volatility (wide spread) periods, since the bid is drawing the price, you are not theoretically losing money on the spread by entering the trade (you'll cover later, with a smaller spread).

Gaps are actually the hardest thing to trade, they are too unpredictable and very very broker dependent. Ultimately gapping is entirely dependent on the broker Liquidity and the number of banks used in their price stream.

Hi Everyone,  
  
Since posting at the start of page 1, I have changed my strategy on weekend gaps. For longer term profits, as suggested by Muntu a while back, the best strategy is to trade with the gap i.e. if it gaps down...go short & vice versa.  
  
Does anyone have an EA coded to trade with the gap? If so, I'd like to optimise various currency pairs to find the best SL/TP for each pair and publish my findings.  
  
With other EAs, I've found it quite useful to be able to place pending orders, to enter the trade only when it shows a conviction in the desired direction, so I think this would be a desirable feature too.  
  
Attached is 2 week data for August 2013.  
  
Cheers,  
  
  
Mike

#  [](/thread/176854-gap-trading)Gap Trading 

  * 

  * [#381](/thread/post/6902762#post6902762 "Post Permalink")

  * Aug 19, 2013 8:00pm  Aug 19, 2013 8:00pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar98258_3.gif) Muntu](muntu)

  * | Joined Mar 2009  | Status: Trader | [448 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=98258)

My friend Blott, I am attaching a chart of the present behavior of the bund after a gap at the open this morning. Since a couple of months I am gravitating towards Market profile and Tape reading as my main tools.  
As you can see, have you gone short right then you'd have had some trouble coming out profitable. But had you waited for it to revisit some previous zones, you could have gotten some clues as to which direction to take. I've come to the conclusion that as with all decision aids in trading, there is no sure fire rule, TIMING IN CONTEXT IS ALWAYS KING.  
Actually, there is something that dictates its law even in the face of a gap and that is the previous level: open, close, value areas, Poc 's of past days/weeks. I have marked some for you to see . I am sure you can have similar situations on your own charts.  
As for statistics, make sure you have at least 20 occurrences before drawing a conclusion.  
As for an EA, I know nothing about them and will continue to try without. The best EA you can dream of is between pour 2 eyes. It only requests you to think in probabilities, provided you have an edge.  
  
Best

  * [#382](/thread/post/6904759#post6904759 "Post Permalink")

  * Aug 20, 2013 3:51pm  Aug 20, 2013 3:51pm 

  * [ blott](blott)

  * | Joined Jul 2009  | Status: Trader | [238 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=109256) | Online Now 

Hi Muntu,  
Thanks for taking the time to share your thoughts, and for your charts. I have to reluctantly agree with you (not because I don't want to, but because I fell for all the hype that we are all bombarded with by shysters, that an EA will make you rich overnight; only the vendor becomes night overnight!) that the best EA is between our ears!  
I am also coming to the conclusion that trading with the gap is not the panacea I thought it would be![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f612.png?v=15.1)As we progress through our trading journey, we discard various indicators and ideas that don't work (for us) and slowly come to an understanding of what really moves the market (apart from fear & greed), and in my opinion that is:- a. where the bank customers buy/sell orders are and b. that the banks periodically have to re-balance their currencies, otherwise they end up with too much of one currency, leaving them overexposed like a store keeper with too much of one product! Not forgetting volume, of course, the one indicator that the banks cannot fool us with, as it costs them to fake volume!  
  
You may like to visit the Metaquotes site articles about cluster indicators <http://articles.mql4.com/484> and <http://www.mql4.com/search#!keyword=cluster> Some interesting stuff there. I attach a pic showing an example of cluster indicators in action. You will see from Powerlines indicator that the USD is coming down and AUD has flattened out, and from CC that USD and AUD are moving towards each other. Hopefully they will intersect (where there will be indecision) and hopefully they will continue in opposite directions.  
  
This is a bit off-topic for gap trading, so I may start a new thread.  
  
Regards
